2:31:1696:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:32:1704:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Time-inconsistency of no-bailout policies can create incentives for banks to take excessive risks and
2:33:1805:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:generate endogenous crises when the government cannot commit. However, at the outbreak of financial
2:34:1904:14:14:72:539:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:problems, usually the government is uncertain about their nature, and hence it may delay intervention to
2:35:2008:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:learn more about them. We show that intervention delay leads to strategic restraint banks endogenously
2:36:2110:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:restrict the riskiness of their portfolio relative to their peers in order to avoid being the worst performers
2:37:2220:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and bearing the cost of such delay. These novel forces help to avoid endogenous crises even when
2:38:2316:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:the government cannot commit. We analyze the effect of government policies from the perspective
2:39:2411:14:42:72:158:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:of this new result.
2:40:2430:42:14:72:140:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Jaromir Nosal
2:41:2443:14:14:72:185:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Economics Department
2:42:2463:14:14:72:173:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Columbia University

3:59:2813:57:20:281:329:538:119:g_d0_f7:119:g_d0_f7:?:Abstract
3:60:2821:20:14:117:510:518:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:Time-inconsistency of no-bailout policies can create incentives for banks to take
3:61:2902:14:13:101:510:504:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:excessive risks and generate endogenous crises when the government cannot commit.
3:62:2983:13:14:101:511:491:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:However, at the outbreak of financial problems, usually the government is uncertain
3:63:3066:14:13:101:511:477:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:about their nature, and hence it may delay intervention to learn more about them. We
3:64:3150:13:14:101:510:464:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:show that intervention delay leads tostrategic restraint: banks endogenously restrict
3:65:3235:14:14:101:511:450:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:the riskiness of their portfolio relative to their peers in order to avoid being the worst
3:66:3325:14:13:101:510:436:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:performers and bearing the cost of such delay. These novel forces help to avoid en-
3:67:3408:13:14:101:510:423:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:dogenous crises even when the government cannot commit. We analyze the e↵ect of
3:68:3487:14:45:101:386:409:119:g_d0_f8:119:g_d0_f8:A:government policies from the perspective of this new result.
3:69:3547:45:30:72:208:364:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:1  Introduction
3:70:3562:30:18:72:540:334:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Few would disagree that bailouts are socially costly. Yet, they are commonly used to help
3:71:3651:18:17:72:540:316:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks and financial institutions during crises in most countries, dating as far back as the
3:72:3742:17:18:72:540:299:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:1800s.1In the recent 2008-09 financial crisis, for example, the U.S. government used a
3:73:3828:18:18:71:539:281:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:variety of instruments to bail out, on an unprecedented scale, many financial entities that
3:74:3919:18:18:71:225:263:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:were exposed to systemic risk.
3:75:3949:18:16:85:539:245:49:g_d0_f13:99:g_d0_f8:F:⇤We thank Mark Aguiar, Marco Bassetto, Philip Bond, V.V. Chari, Hal Cole, Emmanuel Farhi, Mike
3:76:4043:16:12:72:540:229:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Golosov, Gary Gorton, Oleg Itskhoki, Bob King, Nobu Kiyotaki, Svetlana Pevnitskaya, Richard Rogerson,
3:77:4144:12:12:72:540:217:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Esteban Rossi-Hansberg, Alp Simsek, Jean Tirole, Jonathan Vogel and Warren Weber for helpful comments,
3:78:4246:12:12:72:540:205:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:as well as seminar participants at Boston College, Boston University, Chicago Fed, Columbia, Florida State
3:79:4352:12:12:72:540:193:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:University, Harvard, National Bank of Poland, Minneapolis Fed, Notre Dame, Penn State, Princeton, St.
3:80:4453:12:12:72:540:181:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Louis Fed, Toulouse School of Economics, University of Pennsylvania, Wharton, the Roma Macro Junior
3:81:4552:12:11:72:540:169:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Conference at the EIEF, the SED 2012 Annual Meetings in Cyprus and the LAEF Conference at Santa
3:82:4647:11:9:72:304:158:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Barbara. The usual waiver of responsibilities applies.
3:83:4701:9:12:85:181:149:49:g_d0_f14:99:g_d0_f8:A:†Columbia University.
3:84:4722:12:12:85:259:137:49:g_d0_f14:99:g_d0_f8:A:‡University of Pennsylvania and NBER.
3:85:4759:12:15:85:539:125:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:1In 1857, after the Livingston vs. Bank of New York case, for example, courts ordered that ‘the mere
3:86:4859:15:12:72:540:110:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:fact of suspension of specie payments when it is general is not of itself su-cient proof of fraud or injustice’,
3:87:4971:12:0:72:507:98:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:o-cially sanctioning suspensions of specie payments in case of aggregate crises and systemic events.
4:88:5072:0:18:89:539:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:An extensive literature, most recently represented by Farhi and Tirole (2012), provides an
4:89:5162:18:18:71:539:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:explanation for this phenomenon based on moral hazard–driven excessive leverage of banks,
4:90:5251:18:18:71:539:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:triggered by the time inconsistency of no-bailout policies. If the government faces certain
4:91:5342:18:18:71:539:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:losses due to bank failures in case of a shock – there may not be enough liquidity in the
4:92:5431:18:18:71:539:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:system because of a systemic nature of the shock, for example – then it may be tempted
4:93:5517:18:18:71:539:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to bail out banks in distress ex post. Without commitment, banks internalize this ex-post
4:94:5606:18:18:71:539:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:reaction and hence have no incentive to avoid exposing themselves to such shocks ex ante,
4:95:5695:18:18:71:540:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:e↵ectively creating crises endogenously. This leads to equilibrium outcomes that are away
4:96:5784:18:18:71:539:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:from the social optimum (in which the government commits to no bailouts, hence disciplining
4:97:5875:18:18:71:307:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank actions and avoiding endogenous crises).
4:98:5920:18:18:89:540:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Two important assumptions underlying these results are perfect observability of the state
4:99:6009:18:18:71:539:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of the economy – the shocks are public information, and degenerate timing of events –
4:100:6094:18:17:71:539:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:all banks fail or survive at the same time. However, casual observation of crises episodes
4:101:6184:17:18:71:539:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:reveals that neither is satisfied in practice. The outbreak of most financial crises is rarely
4:102:6278:18:18:71:539:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:characterized by all financial institutions suddenly and simultaneously showing distress. As
4:103:6370:18:18:71:539:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:a result, policymakers are usually uncertain whether they are facing an isolated incident
4:104:6459:18:18:71:539:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of distress, which can be solved internally in the financial system through mergers and
4:105:6546:18:18:71:539:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:acquisitions, or a more systemic event, in which output may be lost without government
4:106:6632:18:18:71:539:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:intervention. Hence, at least at the onset of a financial crisis, bailout decisions are taken
4:107:6725:18:18:71:539:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:under conditions of uncertainty, with government observing only imperfect signals of the
4:108:6813:18:18:71:432:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:severity of the problem: we call this situationgovernment uncertainty.
4:109:6883:18:18:89:539:330:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In the most recent crisis, for example, when U.S. policymakers decided not to bail out
4:110:6969:18:18:71:539:312:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Lehman Brothers on September 14, 2008, allowing the company to file for bankruptcy in the
4:111:7058:18:18:71:539:294:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:hopes that another company would take over, they were criticized for putting the financial
4:112:7148:18:18:71:539:276:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:system on the brink of a collapse. However, this decision was in part motivated by uncertainty
4:113:7242:18:18:71:539:258:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:about the nature of the underlying problem and by the hope that the financial system would
4:114:7332:18:17:71:539:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:restore normality without relying on costly public intervention.2The bailout of Continental
4:115:7423:17:18:72:540:223:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Illinois Bank and Trust Company in 1984 provides another example. The FDIC chairman
4:116:7506:18:18:72:539:205:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:at the time, William Isaac, explained that ‘the best estimates of our sta↵,with the sparse
4:117:7596:18:18:72:543:187:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f5:B:numbers we had at hand,werethatmorethan2,000banksmightbethreatenedorbrought
4:118:7671:18:18:72:539:169:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:down by a Continental collapse.’3This anecdotal evidence suggests that bailout decisions are
4:119:7763:18:18:72:540:151:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:usually made under conditions of uncertainty, fueled by governments’ limitations to acquire
4:120:7854:18:15:85:539:133:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:2Kelly, Lustig, and Van Nieuwerburgh (2011) provide a thorough discussion of the timing of events and
4:121:7955:15:9:72:426:118:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the evolution of government’s announcements of bailouts during the recent crisis.
4:122:8036:9:0:85:192:109:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:A:3Our emphasis in italics.
5:123:8062:0:18:72:190:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:or process information.
5:124:8085:18:18:89:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The main result of this paper is thatgovernment uncertaintyhas the potential for sus-
5:125:8170:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:taining commitment outcomes even when the government lacks commitment. Intuitively,
5:126:8253:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:at the onset of financial problems, governments are uncertain about their systemic nature,
5:127:8343:18:18:72:539:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:and hence about the actual need for a bailout. In order to observe more signals andlearn
5:128:8431:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:about the nature of the shock, the government may want todelay bailoutand let the first
5:129:8518:18:18:72:540:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank(s) in distress fail – with learning allowing it to avoid an unnecessary and potentially
5:130:8610:18:18:72:540:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:costly intervention. Crucially, intervention delay makes the relative performance of banks’
5:131:8701:18:18:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:portfolios critical for individual banks, since no bank wants to be amongst the first in line
5:132:8794:18:18:72:544:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:for government help. We call this e↵ectstrategic restraint,asbanksendogenouslyrestrict
5:133:8880:18:18:72:540:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the riskiness of their portfolio relative to their peers in order to avoid being amongst the
5:134:8972:18:18:72:483:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:worst performers, inducing a sort of competition to reduce excessive risk-taking.
5:135:9053:18:17:89:539:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In the model, bankers borrow short-term from households to finance projects that are
5:136:9137:17:18:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:illiquid. Projects may su↵er shocks over time, in which case they require extra funds to bring
5:137:9231:18:18:72:540:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:them to fruition. The shock hitting a project may be idiosyncratic, hitting only certain banks,
5:138:9326:18:18:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:or aggregate, hitting all banks. High levels of short-term debt allow banks to invest in large
5:139:9420:18:18:72:540:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:projects, but at the same time hinder their ability to refinance if a shock hits. We study the
5:140:9514:18:18:72:543:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:problem of a central authority, which we call thegovernment,whichmaximizestotalwelfare
5:141:9600:18:18:72:539:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:(bankers’ plus households’) using an interest rate policy that a↵ects the cost of borrowing to
5:142:9694:18:18:72:540:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:refinance in case of shocks. An intervention that reduces the cost of borrowing to bankers,
5:143:9785:18:18:72:545:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:which we call abailout,isfinancedthroughtaxesonhouseholdsinawaythatissocially
5:144:9862:18:18:72:540:330:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:costly (e.g. due to distortions). The benefits of bailouts, on the other hand, are naturally
5:145:9954:18:18:72:447:312:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:given by bringing banks’ projects to fruition, and thus increasing output.
5:146:10028:18:18:89:539:294:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:When the government observes a bank in distress – which we define as the bank running
5:147:10113:18:18:72:540:276:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:out of cash and options for refinancing on the market – it does not observe whether the shock
5:148:10206:18:18:72:540:258:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is idiosyncratic or aggregate, information that is critical for taking appropriate action. If the
5:149:10303:18:18:72:540:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shock is idiosyncratic, other banks have enough liquidity to take over the distressed bank,
5:150:10394:18:17:72:540:222:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and no intervention is needed. If the shock is aggregate, intervention is the only way to avoid
5:151:10489:17:18:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:a project failure. Hence, the government’s decision to bail out the bank or not depends on
5:152:10579:18:18:72:280:187:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:its beliefs about the nature of the shock.
5:153:10621:18:18:89:539:169:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We show that, if the government is initially relatively optimistic it is not facing an
5:154:10707:18:18:72:540:151:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate shock, then it chooses to learn more by delaying intervention, not bailing out the
5:155:10799:18:18:72:540:133:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:first distressed bank(s). By delaying the bailout, the government maintains the option of
5:156:10888:18:18:72:540:115:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:introducing the bailout at a later time – after observing subsequent signals (further bank
5:157:10978:18:0:72:540:97:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:distress) – under a more precise belief about the true state. For the banks, on the other
6:158:11068:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:hand, delay introduces an incentive to avoid being the worst performers. In the model, this
6:159:11159:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:happens through banks leveraging less and carrying more cash reserves than its peers for
6:160:11247:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the eventuality of being hit by the refinancing shock, at the cost of downsizing its project.
6:161:11340:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:This is thestrategic restrainte↵ect, which gives Bertrand-style competition among banks
6:162:11427:18:18:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:for lower leverage. We show that in the unique equilibrium of the economy, banks compete
6:163:11515:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:away all excessive leverage, and the allocation coincides with the one which obtains under
6:164:11605:18:18:72:503:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:commitment, here driven by government uncertainty and strategic restraint instead.
6:165:11687:18:18:89:539:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In our benchmark, we consider a stark case in which banks can guarantee not being the
6:166:11772:18:18:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:worst performer by choosing slightly lower leverage relative to other banks.  Our results,
6:167:11862:18:18:72:540:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:however, are robust to relaxing this assumption. In an extended environment, we consider
6:168:11950:18:18:72:540:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shocks to cash holdings of individual banks, such that small deviations in leverage do not
6:169:12040:18:18:72:539:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:guarantee outperfoming other banks. In this case, we show that thegovernment uncertainty
6:170:12128:18:17:72:540:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:andstrategic restraintforces still operate, moving the equilibrium allocation towards the op-
6:171:12221:17:18:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:timal (commitment) outcome. In this case, however, the unique equilibrium achieves leverage
6:172:12312:18:18:72:540:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:that is intermediate between the commitment (optimal) and non-commitment (ine-cient)
6:173:12396:18:18:72:362:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium, the benchmark model being a limiting case.
6:174:12451:18:18:89:539:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Given thatgovernment uncertaintyandstrategic restraintforces robustly implement allo-
6:175:12536:18:18:72:540:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:cations that dominate the non-commitment equilibrium in terms of welfare (the benchmark
6:176:12623:18:18:72:540:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:achieving the optimum), natural policy questions arise regarding the e↵ect of regulation and
6:177:12715:18:18:72:539:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:economic environment on the e↵ectiveness of these e↵ects. How does financial innovation
6:178:12802:18:18:72:539:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:a↵ect uncertainty and the likelihood of endogenous crises? Is government uncertainty more
6:179:12891:18:18:72:540:330:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:e↵ective when there are many banks? Is it more e↵ective when banks are of similar size?
6:180:12978:18:18:72:280:312:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:We address these questions in the paper.
6:181:13018:18:18:89:538:294:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We model financial innovation as a↵ecting the ability of banks to insure away part of their
6:182:13109:18:18:71:539:276:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:idiosyncratic risk, for example by trading securitized products or over-the-counter deriva-
6:183:13200:18:18:71:539:258:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:tives.  In the benchmark model, any level of insurance introduces di↵erences in the cash
6:184:13288:18:18:72:540:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:position of banks which depend on the type of shocks: when the shock is idiosyncratic, the
6:185:13378:18:17:72:539:222:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:a↵ected bank has more cash to refinance because it has claims on healthy projects of other
6:186:13468:17:18:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks. This di↵erence in cash translates into a clear di↵erence between idiosyncratic and
6:187:13557:18:18:72:540:187:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate shocks in when the bank is going to run out of cash and financing options, and
6:188:13645:18:18:72:540:169:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:hence when it is going to show distress. In the benchmark, cash and time of distress are
6:189:13733:18:18:72:540:151:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:deterministically connected, and hence the government can perfectly infer the shock from
6:190:13821:18:18:72:540:133:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the time the bank becomes distressed. Hence, perhaps surprisingly, we show that in the
6:191:13907:18:18:72:539:115:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:benchmark model, foranylevel of insurance, imperfect information plays no role and the
6:192:13993:18:0:71:539:97:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium of the economy coincides with one with no government uncertainty, leading to
7:193:14082:0:18:72:434:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:an ine-cient equilibrium allocation (the non-commitement allocation).
7:194:14151:18:18:89:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:This result hinges on the ability to perfectly infer the underlying state from the time the
7:195:14242:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank becomes distressed, which is relaxed in our extended environment discussed earlier.
7:196:14330:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:With shocks to cash holdings, the government knows only theaveragetime of distress under
7:197:14418:18:18:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:idiosyncratic and aggregate shocks, and hence the inference from the actual time of distress to
7:198:14513:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the underlying shock is imperfect. This preserves the government uncertainty and strategic
7:199:14603:18:18:72:539:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:restraint forces in economies with su-ciently imperfect insurance. In particular, we derive
7:200:14694:18:18:71:539:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:a cap on the fraction of idiosyncratic risk that can be insured away, which still allows for
7:201:14786:18:18:71:539:563:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f5:B:government uncertaintyto lead to welfare-superior allocations. We find the cap to be an
7:202:14873:18:18:71:539:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:increasing function of the variance of the shocks to cash holdings. These results point to
7:203:14963:18:18:71:539:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:an unexplored e↵ect of financial innovation, such as securitization, in that it hinders the
7:204:15054:18:18:71:540:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:e↵ectiveness of government uncertainty and strategic restraint in implementing commitment
7:205:15143:18:17:71:539:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:outcomes, by reducing the government’s value of delaying the bailout and learning. This
7:206:15230:17:18:71:376:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:suggests a new rationale for regulating financial innovation.
7:207:15291:18:18:89:538:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We also explore the role of industry concentration, measured by the number of banks.
7:208:15375:18:18:71:539:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:A larger number of banks strengthens our two forces that induce governments to delay
7:209:15459:18:18:71:539:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:intervention. First, governments become more optimistic that there exists a healthy bank
7:210:15547:18:18:71:539:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:able to take over a bank in distress. Second, there is a larger option value of learning the
7:211:15639:18:18:71:539:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:true state, by allowing the first bank in distress to fail, and making better decisions later
7:212:15732:18:18:71:539:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:for a larger number of banks. The overall result is that decreasing industry concentration
7:213:15822:18:18:71:347:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:makes commitment outcomes more easily sustainable.
7:214:15872:18:18:89:540:330:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Finally, we study the e↵ect of bank size heterogeneity. When a single bank is asymmet-
7:215:15958:18:18:71:539:312:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:rically large in the industry, it is less likely that it can be acquired by its peers and hence
7:216:16053:18:18:71:539:294:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:more likely that the government must bail it out in case of distress, even if it is the first bank
7:217:16151:18:18:71:540:276:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:experiencing problems. Hence, with su-cient asymmetry in bank size, large banks do not
7:218:16237:18:18:72:540:258:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:have any concern for their relative performance and choose excessive leverage. Given this
7:219:16326:18:18:72:540:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:behavior, smaller banks have a strategic incentive to increase their leverage relative their
7:220:16418:18:17:72:540:222:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:leverage in the symmetric case: they choose to expose themselves only slightly less than the
7:221:16510:17:18:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:large bank. In our setting, the ‘too big to fail’ problem shows up very di↵erently than in the
7:222:16604:18:18:72:540:187:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:rest of the literature because large banks become shields for smaller banks to take excessive
7:223:16697:18:18:72:540:169:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:risk, exerting a negative externality on the economy by inducing endogenous systemic crises
7:224:16788:18:30:72:176:151:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of larger magnitude.
7:225:16808:30:18:89:540:121:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f5:A:Related LiteratureThere is a large literature on the time-consistency of the no bailout
7:226:16895:18:0:72:540:103:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:policies and moral hazard behavior of banks, to which this paper contributes. A number of
8:227:16985:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:papers, extensively reviewed in Stern and Feldman (2004), argue that the existence of ‘too
8:228:17075:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:big to fail’ banks is the source of the time inconsistency of policies, and at the root of crises.
8:229:17173:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Another strand of the literature, most recently represented by Acharya and Yorulmazer
8:230:17258:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:(2007), Pasten (2011) and especially Farhi and Tirole (2012) argue that ’too big to fail’
8:231:17347:18:18:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks are not necessary and coordinated actions by smaller banks give rise to endogenous
8:232:17435:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:crises too. The results in this paper apply in both environments, always working towards
8:233:17523:18:18:72:496:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:putting more discipline on bank actions and achieving welfare-superior allocations.
8:234:17606:18:18:89:540:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Our setting builds on Holmstr ̈om and Tirole (1998) and Farhi and Tirole (2012). Relative
8:235:17695:18:18:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to their work, we introduce idiosyncratic shocks and the possibility of government uncertainty
8:236:17789:18:18:72:540:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:about the nature of the shock. We additionally allow for e-cient takeovers of distressed
8:237:17877:18:18:72:540:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks by healthy banks, making the true nature of the shock crucial for the government. In
8:238:17967:18:18:72:533:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:contrast to their work, the timing of bank distress at the onset of a crisis is critical for us.
8:239:18063:18:17:89:540:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Our work also relates to Acharya and Yorulmazer (2007), who develop a model of ‘too-
8:240:18147:17:18:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:many to fail’ in an environment where bank takeovers are also possible and technologically
8:241:18237:18:18:72:540:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:superior to bailouts, as in our paper.  In our model, the ‘wait and see’ strategy of the
8:242:18325:18:18:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:government has the additional gain of providing information to the government about the
8:243:18412:18:18:72:540:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:nature of the shocks, which createsstrategic restraintand hinders the possibility of herding
8:244:18504:18:18:72:172:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:that they highlight.
8:245:18524:18:18:89:539:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Recently, Green (2010) and Keister (2011) argue that bailouts may be optimal to avoid
8:246:18609:18:18:72:540:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:excessive hoarding of liquidity. In a similar vein, Cheng and Milbradt (2010) suggest bailouts
8:247:18703:18:18:72:540:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:can instill confidence on credit markets. In our setup, whatever the optimal level of liquidity
8:248:18798:18:18:72:540:330:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is, it can be attained as long as government uncertainty and strategic restraint forces are at
8:249:18892:18:18:72:288:312:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:work, even in the absence of commitment.
8:250:18932:18:18:89:539:294:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Bianchi (2012) concludes that moral hazard e↵ects of bailouts are significantly mitigated
8:251:19021:18:18:72:540:276:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:by making bailouts contingent on the occurrence of a systemic financial crisis. In contrast,
8:252:19113:18:18:72:540:258:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:in our framework shocks are unobservable and hence the government cannot make bailouts
8:253:19199:18:18:72:540:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:contingent upon them. This gives rise to a positive option of delay and learning, which is
8:254:19289:18:17:72:329:222:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:exactly what mitigates the moral hazard problem.
8:255:19337:17:18:89:539:205:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Davila (2012) also argues, as in our extension to asymmetric bank sizes, that large banks
8:256:19426:18:18:72:540:187:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:allow small banks to take more risks, making the economy-wide leverage and probability of
8:257:19515:18:18:72:540:169:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bailouts larger when large banks are present. While his results are based on banks’ uncer-
8:258:19605:18:18:72:540:151:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:tainty about bailout policies, ours depend on governments’ uncertainty about the nature of
8:259:19695:18:18:72:128:133:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the shocks.
8:260:19706:18:18:89:544:115:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Arecentstrandoftheliteraturehighlightsthee↵ectsofpolicyuncertaintyininducing
8:261:19782:18:0:72:540:97:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:crises and delaying recoveries. Cukierman and Izhakian (2011), for example, show that un-
9:262:19872:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:certainty about policymakers’s actions can induce sudden financial collapses when investors
9:263:19963:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:follow a max-min behavior. Baker, Bloom, and Davis (2012) argue that uncertainty about
9:264:20049:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:future policies delays recoveries since individuals prefer to ’wait and see.’ In our case, it
9:265:20142:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is the government who is uncertain about the nature of refinancing shocks and may like to
9:266:20231:18:18:72:473:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:’wait and see’ before intervening, reducing the likelihood of endogenous crises.
9:267:20311:18:18:89:539:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Finally, there is a previous literature that explores the ability of imperfect information
9:268:20401:18:18:72:540:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to improve equilibrium outcomes under time inconsistency. Cremer (1995) shows in a static
9:269:20490:18:18:72:540:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:game that the inability of a principal to observe workers’ types can serve as a commitment
9:270:20580:18:18:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:device to punishing low output realizations, while Carrillo and Mariotti (2000) show that
9:271:20669:18:18:72:540:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:an agent with time-inconsistent preferences might optimally choose not to learn in order to
9:272:20760:18:18:72:540:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:restrict future selves. The e↵ect of imperfect information in our model has a similar flavor,
9:273:20853:18:18:72:540:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:but in our banking setting, the competition that arises from the banks’ concerns for their
9:274:20943:18:17:72:540:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:relative position is critical for our results, and is absent in their settings. Furthermore, our
9:275:21039:17:18:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:setting is dynamic, and the government not only delays because of imperfect information
9:276:21126:18:18:72:519:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:but also because there are gains from learning and resolving the imperfect information.
9:277:21213:18:18:89:539:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In what follows, we first set up a simple analytical example in order to illustrate the main
9:278:21305:18:18:72:540:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:forces behind our arguments. Then, we provide a micro-founded model of these forces, first
9:279:21395:18:18:72:540:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:analyzing the model under full information as a benchmark and then introducing imperfect
9:280:21483:18:18:72:540:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:information to derive our main results. Next, we discuss policy implications. Finally, we
9:281:21572:18:45:72:322:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:conclude and discuss avenues for future research.
9:282:21621:45:30:72:238:321:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:2  Simple Example
9:283:21638:30:18:72:540:291:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Consider an economy with two banking entrepreneurs (banks or firms more generally) that
9:284:21725:18:18:72:542:273:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:live for three periods. Att=0,eachbankisendowedwithaprojectandaunitofnumeraire,
9:285:21804:18:18:72:543:255:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:that we will callcash, which can be used for consumption or savings. Att=1,eachproject
9:286:21890:18:18:71:540:237:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:can either be successful, payingY>1, or in distress, needing additional funds to continue
9:287:21979:18:18:71:545:219:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and to payYatt=2. Weassumebothprojectsareindistress(aggregate shock)with
9:288:22051:18:17:72:539:201:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:B:probabilityP2,onlyoneprojectisindistress(idiosyncratic shock) with probability 2P1
9:289:22133:17:18:72:540:184:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and no project is in distress with probabilityP0. Refinancing the whole distressed project
9:290:22223:18:18:72:475:166:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:requires a unit of cash and it is not possible to increase the size of the project.
9:291:22306:18:18:89:539:148:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f18:A:Att=0thebankcansaveafractioncof the endowed cash to refinance up to a fractionc
9:292:22385:18:18:71:540:130:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of a distressed project. We assume cash can only be consumed att= 0 or used for refinancing
9:293:22476:18:18:71:544:112:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the project att= 1. Hence, conditional on savingc,theexpectedpayo↵forthebankis
9:294:22554:18:0:71:438:94:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f5:B:Y-cif the project is successful andcY-cif the project is in distress.
10:295:22624:0:18:89:539:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We assume that, in case of an idiosyncratic shock, thehealthy bank(the one with a
10:296:22705:18:18:71:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:successful project) can make a take-it-or-leave-it o↵er for the distressed project, using the
10:297:22798:18:18:71:542:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:proceedings from its own project. Since the healthy bank receivesY>1ofcashatt=1,it
10:298:22880:18:18:71:539:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:has enough resources to refinance the distressed project fully. In this situation, the healthy
10:299:22974:18:18:71:539:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank pays 1-cto reap the full benefit equal to (1-c)Yfrom the part of the project the
10:300:23059:18:18:72:333:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:distressed bank cannot refinance with own savings.
10:301:23109:18:18:89:539:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:There is also a government in the economy that can contribute to refinance an additional
10:302:23197:18:18:72:545:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:fractioncGof the project, such thatc+cG1. We call this contribution abailout.Abailout
10:303:23283:18:18:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is implemented by transferring funds with social costs that are proportional to the size of
10:304:23374:18:18:72:543:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the transfer,cGT.Wealsoassumebailoutsareundirected–onceo↵ered,healthybanksalso
10:305:23452:18:18:72:515:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:have access to the bailout and can consumecGfrom a transfer that socially costscGT.
10:306:23535:18:17:89:544:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We will denote byy=Y-1thesocialgainfromrefinancingwithprivatefunds,by
10:307:23604:17:18:71:538:492:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:F:x=Y-Tthe social gain from refinancing with public funds (bailouts), and bybx=1-T
10:308:23684:18:18:71:539:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the social gain from a transfer to a healthy bank.  We assume that bailouts are socially
10:309:23772:18:18:71:539:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:costly (raising public funds introduces distortions) but beneficial (bailouts save socially useful
10:310:23870:18:28:71:497:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:projects). This is summarized in Assumption A, which implies thaty>x>0>bx.
10:311:23944:28:28:71:440:410:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:C:Assumption ABailouts are socially costly, but beneficial:1<T <Y.
10:312:24008:28:18:89:539:382:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Below, we first study the case in which the government hasfull informationabout the
10:313:24091:18:18:71:539:364:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:nature of the shocks (whether both, one or no projects are in distress). This benchmark
10:314:24178:18:18:71:539:346:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:highlights how the government’s inability to commit reduces welfare.  Then, we assume
10:315:24263:18:18:71:539:328:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f5:B:imperfect informationabout the nature of shocks and show that the economy can achieve
10:316:24348:18:39:71:462:310:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:commitment outcomes, even when the government is still unable to commit.
10:317:24420:39:25:72:224:271:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:C:2.1  Full Information
10:318:24441:25:26:72:212:246:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f11:C:2.1.1  No Commitment
10:319:24461:26:18:72:540:220:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In this section we assume the government is unable to commit to any policy announced at

10:321:24599:18:18:89:543:184:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The government never intervenes in the case of an idiosyncratic shock. Sincey>x,the
10:322:24682:18:18:71:539:166:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:distressed project can be taken over and refinanced by the healthy bank without distortions.
10:323:24774:18:18:71:540:148:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In contrast, the government always intervenes in the case of an aggregate shock. Sincex>0
10:324:24863:18:18:71:457:130:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:it is preferred to refinance the project at a social cost than let it disappear.

13:389:28767:0:28:89:527:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The following lemma summarizes the discussion for the full information environment.
13:390:28850:28:18:71:540:679:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Lemma 1With full information and under Assumptions A - D, the equilibrium is unique
13:391:28933:18:18:71:539:661:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:and characterized as follows:(i)when governments can commit, banks save to full refinancing
13:392:29024:18:18:71:539:643:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:(c=1) and bailouts never happen on the equilibrium path,(ii)when governments cannot
13:393:29107:18:18:71:540:625:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:commit, banks do not save (c=0) and bailouts happen in case of aggregate shocks. Moreover,
13:394:29197:18:39:71:266:607:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:(i)dominates(ii)in terms of welfare.
13:395:29233:39:26:72:266:568:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:C:2.2  Imperfect Information
13:396:29259:26:17:72:540:542:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In this section, we maintain the assumption of no commitment, relax the assumption of
13:397:29344:17:18:72:545:525:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:government’s full information about the nature of shocks att=1,andderiveourmain
13:398:29423:18:18:71:543:507:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:result. First, we assume banks show distressin sequence,withthebankwiththelowestcash
13:399:29507:18:18:71:539:489:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:savings showing distress first if su↵ering a need of refinancing.4Second, the government only
13:400:29600:18:18:72:540:471:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:observes whether a given project is in distress, but not the nature of the shock (aggregate
13:401:29691:18:18:72:179:453:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:versus idiosyncratic).
13:402:29713:18:18:89:539:435:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:When the government observes a bank’s project in distress, it does not know whether
13:403:29796:18:18:72:540:417:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the project of the other bank is also in distress (such that both projects will eventually
13:404:29886:18:18:72:540:399:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:need refinancing), or not (such that the healthy bank has enough resources to take over
13:405:29973:18:18:72:540:381:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the distressed project and e-ciently refinance it with private funds). However, observing a
13:406:30064:18:18:72:540:363:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank’s project in distress is a valuable signal, and it leads to the government updating the
13:407:30156:18:34:72:354:345:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:probability of an aggregate shock, using Bayes’ rule, to
13:408:30212:34:0:255:280:311:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f5:?:P02=
13:409:30216:0:16:298:309:319:143:g_d0_f18:64:g_d0_f12:?:P2
13:410:30218:16:0:284:323:303:143:g_d0_f18:64:g_d0_f12:?:P1+P2
13:411:30223:0:34:328:540:311:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f5:A:>P2.(3)
13:412:30230:34:33:72:464:277:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:If the government bails out the first bank in distress, the expected welfare is
13:413:30309:33:33:245:366:244:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:C:P022x+(1-P02)(x+bx).
13:414:30329:33:18:71:539:211:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In words, if the shock is aggregate the government saves both projects but if the shock
13:415:30416:18:18:71:539:193:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is idiosyncratic, the government saves the distressed project with public funds (which is
13:416:30505:18:18:71:540:175:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ine-cient, since it would have been taken over in the absence of a bailout), and ine-ciently
13:417:30597:18:18:71:525:157:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:provides public funds to the healthy bank (since bailouts are assumed to be undirected).
13:418:30685:18:16:85:540:139:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:4When banks initially save the samec, we assume as a tie breaking rule that each bank has a probability
13:419:30788:16:12:72:539:123:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:1/2 of showing distress first. The relationship between cashcand the order of showing distress is assumed
13:420:30893:12:0:72:328:111:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:in the simple economy, and later derived in the full model.
14:421:30954:0:33:89:523:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:If the government does not bail out the first bank in distress, the expected welfare is
14:422:31041:33:33:263:348:674:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:C:P02x+(1-P02)y.
14:423:31055:33:18:72:540:641:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In words, if the shock is aggregate the government loses the first project (the government can
14:424:31149:18:18:72:540:623:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:always bailout the second project if also showing distress) but if the shock is idiosyncratic the
14:425:31246:18:18:72:539:605:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:government induces a takeover (which is the most e-cient refinancing alternative) and avoids
14:426:31338:18:18:72:539:587:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ine-cient public transfers to the healthy bank. This expression then captures the static and
14:427:31430:18:18:72:540:569:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:dynamic gains from delaying governments’ intervention. The static part is avoiding a mistake
14:428:31522:18:17:72:540:551:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:with the first distressed bank. The dynamic part is the value of learning the nature of the
14:429:31613:17:18:72:389:534:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shock and not providing ine-cient transfers to healthy banks.
14:430:31674:18:18:89:544:516:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:If the government is certain that the shock is aggregate (i.e.P02=1),thenitalways
14:431:31755:18:18:71:539:498:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:prefers to bail out the first bank in distress (since 2x>x).  On the other hand, if the
14:432:31842:18:18:71:544:480:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:government is certain that the shock is idiosyncratic (i.e.P02=0),thenitneverprefersto
14:433:31928:18:18:72:335:462:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bail out the first bank in distress (sincey>x+bx).
14:434:31978:18:18:89:546:444:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In general, there is a cuto↵ ̄P,suchthatforallP02< ̄P,thegovernmentassignsa

14:436:32146:18:33:72:453:408:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:intervention. Thedelayed bailout conditionfor the government is therefore
14:437:32219:33:0:252:323:375:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f4:?:P02< ̄P⌘1-

14:440:32234:0:34:356:540:375:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f5:A:.(4)
14:441:32238:34:18:89:539:341:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Factors that increase the cuto↵, making it more likely that governments delay intervention

14:444:32518:18:18:89:539:287:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:An important assumption here is that governments cannot help banks little by little,
14:445:32602:18:18:71:539:269:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:maintaining them alive until learning the nature of the shock. Hence, if the shock is aggregate
14:446:32697:18:18:71:515:251:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:B:and governments do not help banks immediately to refinance fully, the project is lost.5
14:447:32784:18:18:89:540:233:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:How do the banks react to the fact that the government is uncertain about the nature of
14:448:32871:18:18:71:539:215:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shocks? If the delayed bailout condition (4) isnotsatisfied, then banks know they would be
14:449:32961:18:18:71:545:197:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bailed out whenever their project is in distress, always obtainingYregardless ofc.Further-
14:450:33051:18:18:71:539:179:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:more, in case of being healthy under an idiosyncratic shock they receive a windfall of public
14:451:33144:18:17:71:539:161:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:transfers that depends on when the other bank shows distress. This implies that, conditional
14:452:33236:17:16:85:539:144:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:5This assumption is certainly realistic for financial intermediaries with very high leverage on overnight

15:490:35354:18:15:85:539:135:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:6Note, however, that this result is independent of Assumption B when information is imperfect.  If

16:501:35976:167:18:89:540:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In essence, even if the government is unable to commit, it can achieve commitment
16:502:36057:18:18:72:540:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:outcomes if it faces uncertainty about the nature of shocks. The main condition for this to
16:503:36148:18:17:72:540:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:happen is that the government remains relatively confident that the shock is idiosyncratic,
16:504:36239:17:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:even after observing a project in distress, and hence delays intervention.  This result is
16:505:36329:18:28:72:235:349:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:summarized in Lemma 2 below.
16:506:36357:28:18:72:540:321:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Lemma 2With imperfect information, no commitment and under Assumptions A - D, the
16:507:36438:18:18:72:540:303:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:equilibrium is unique. IfP02 ̄P, banks save to full refinancing (c=1) and bailouts never
16:508:36527:18:18:72:540:285:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:happen on the equilibrium path, replicating the outcome of full information with commitment.
16:509:36619:18:18:72:539:267:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:IfP02> ̄P, banks do not save (c=0) and bailouts happen when shocks are aggregate, which
16:510:36706:18:28:72:499:249:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:is welfare inferior, replicating the outcome of full information without commitment.
16:511:36790:28:18:89:539:221:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The simple example of this section illustrates the main mechanism behind the e↵ective-
16:512:36876:18:18:72:540:203:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ness of uncertainty in implementing commitment outcomes. However, all functional forms
16:513:36962:18:18:72:540:185:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and assumptions were taken for clarity and tractability. In what follows, we provide a micro-
16:514:37055:18:18:72:540:167:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:founded model of these forces. In particular, we model the benefits and costs of private and
16:515:37147:18:18:72:540:149:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:public liquidity provision and we endogenize both the size of projects and the order in which
16:516:37240:18:0:72:176:131:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks show distress.
17:517:37262:0:30:72:193:707:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:3  Full Model
17:518:37275:30:18:72:540:677:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:The model environment builds on Holmstr ̈om and Tirole (1998) and Farhi and Tirole (2012),
17:519:37365:18:18:72:540:659:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:with several important modifications. First, we introduce two types of shocks, aggregate and
17:520:37457:18:18:72:540:641:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:idiosyncratic, and allow for imperfect information about the nature of the shock. Second,
17:521:37546:18:18:72:540:623:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:we allow for a non-degenerate timing of events, in which banks with higher leverage ratios
17:522:37636:18:18:72:540:605:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:endogenously show distress earlier. Third, we admit the possibility of healthy banks takeover
17:523:37729:18:39:72:158:587:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:distressed banks.
17:524:37746:39:25:72:200:548:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:C:3.1  Environment
17:525:37762:25:18:72:539:523:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Time is continuous and finite,t2[0,2], and there is no discounting. There are three types
17:526:37851:18:18:72:540:505:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of agents in the economy: two banking entrepreneurs (banks hereafter), a continuum of
17:527:37936:18:18:72:540:487:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:households and a government. Banks borrow short-term to finance illiquid projects which
17:528:38023:18:18:72:544:469:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:either pay o↵att=1orneedrefinancingandpayo↵att=2. Abank’sprojectneeds
17:529:38092:18:18:72:540:451:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:refinancing because of an aggregate shock (both banks need refinancing) or an idiosyncratic
17:530:38183:18:18:72:544:433:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shock (only one of the two banks needs refinancing). These shocks hit only at datet=1,
17:531:38269:18:18:72:540:415:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and for the rest of time the economy is deterministic. Households are risk neutral providers
17:532:38361:18:18:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of loans to banks. The government maximizes total welfare, using interest rates and taxes
17:533:38450:18:34:72:302:379:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:on households as its only policy instruments.
17:534:38495:34:26:72:149:345:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f11:C:3.1.1  Banks
17:535:38507:26:18:72:540:319:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:The two banks in the economy have the objective of maximizing their individual net worth,
17:536:38596:18:18:72:539:301:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f5:B:V.Att=0,theychoosethesizeiof an investment project, which is financed using own
17:537:38675:18:18:72:539:283:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:initial assetsAand funds borrowed from the households. The sizeialso determines the speed
17:538:38764:18:18:72:539:265:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of expense outflows (to pay suppliers, workers, etc), which happens at a rateidtduring the
17:539:38854:18:18:72:545:247:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:period, such that all projects run out of funds att=1andlargerprojectshavealarger
17:540:38935:18:18:72:249:229:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:outflow rate than smaller projects.
17:541:38970:18:18:89:539:211:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The payo↵from each project consists of two parts. The first part is deterministic,⇡iat
17:542:39056:18:18:72:543:193:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:timet=1. Thesecondpartisrandom. Iftheprojectdoesnotsu↵eranyshock,itreturns
17:543:39130:18:17:72:540:175:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f18:B:(⇢0+⇢1)iat timet=1,andthebankhasthechoicetoextendtheprojecttosizeji
17:544:39198:17:18:71:543:158:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:which returns ˆ⇢jat timet=2. Iftheprojectsu↵ersashock,itonlypays⇡iat timet=1,
17:545:39275:18:18:72:539:140:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f18:B:and the bank has the choice to refinance the project to sizejiwhich returns (⇢0+⇢1)j
17:546:39360:18:18:72:540:122:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:at timet= 2. Refinancing a project, however, does not change its intrinsic rate of expenses
17:547:39451:18:0:71:539:104:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:outflow – if only half of a large project is refinanced (j=i/2), for example, the bank would
18:548:39545:0:18:72:539:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:run out of cash to pay expenses att=1.5. We introduce financial frictions by assuming that
18:549:39635:18:18:71:539:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:from the total output of the project,⇢1is a benefit that can only be captured by bankers,
18:550:39724:18:18:71:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and hence it is not pledgeble.7This and other parametric assumptions that make the model
18:551:39812:18:31:71:315:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:economically interesting are summarized below.
18:552:39858:31:28:71:345:622:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:C:Assumption 1Assumptions about projects’s payo↵s
18:553:39905:28:28:85:307:594:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:A:1. Binding pledgeability:⇡<1and⇢0<1.
18:554:39941:28:28:85:332:566:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:A:2. E-cient projects:⇡+⇢0+⇢1>1+P1+P2.
18:555:39977:28:28:85:275:538:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:A:3. E-cient refinancing:⇢0+⇢1>1.
18:556:40008:28:30:85:273:510:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:A:4. Ine-cient expansion:⇢0<ˆ⇢<1.
18:557:40039:30:18:89:539:480:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The first part of Assumption 1 guarantees that investment in period 0 is finite, and that
18:558:40128:18:18:72:540:462:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:refinancing depends on retained earnings.  The second part guarantees that running the
18:559:40214:18:18:72:540:444:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:project is ex-ante socially e-cient. The third part guarantees that refinancing the project
18:560:40305:18:18:72:540:426:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is also ex-post socially e-cient. The last part assumes that expansions are ine-cient, but
18:561:40395:18:35:72:321:408:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:privately profitable if the cost of expansion is⇢0.
18:562:40446:35:25:72:283:373:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f11:C:3.1.2  Households and Government
18:563:40478:25:18:72:542:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Acontinuumofhouseholdsbornatt=0ort=1,consumeatt+1andareriskneutral,

18:570:40972:33:18:89:544:192:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The government is benevolent and maximizes welfareW,whichisequaltotheweighted

18:573:41114:18:16:85:539:124:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:7This can be derived from first principles as in Holmstr ̈om and Tirole (1998), for example by moral hazard
18:574:41221:16:0:72:496:108:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:within the bank, in which the banker exerts hidden e↵orts that a↵ect the outcome of the project.
19:575:41319:0:18:89:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:To maximizeWthe government may need to transfer resources from households to banks
19:576:41401:18:18:71:543:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to refinance projects in distress. This is what we call abailout.Theweight-<1introduces
19:577:41488:18:18:71:537:671:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:B:the idea that transfers between households and banks is costly from a welfare perspective.8
19:578:41579:18:18:89:539:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We assume the only policy instrument governments can use to bailout banks, transferring
19:579:41666:18:18:71:539:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:funds from households to bankers is an interest rate policy that determines borrowing costs
19:580:41757:18:18:71:539:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of bankers (i.e.R(t),t2[0,2]) and taxes on households to implement such interest rates.
19:581:41844:18:18:71:543:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:We assume this policy isundirected,whichmeansthatthegovernmentcannotreduceinterest
19:582:41926:18:18:71:539:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:rate only for certain banks and not others. Once a bailout is implemented, all banks can
19:583:42014:18:34:71:491:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:borrow at a lower rate, regardless of whether they had a refinancing shock or not.
19:584:42096:34:26:71:154:529:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f11:C:3.1.3  Timing

19:593:42685:26:18:89:540:352:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f5:A:•If no bank su↵ers the shock, banks choose whether to expand or not, payo↵s are realized
19:594:42773:18:28:101:248:334:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:att=2andthegameends.
19:595:42793:28:18:89:540:306:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f5:A:•If only one bank su↵ers a shock and it shows distress (it may never show distress if it

19:597:42965:18:27:101:193:270:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:to bail out or not.
19:598:42984:27:18:114:540:243:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f5:A:–If the government does not provide a bailout, the healthy bank decides whether
19:599:43063:18:22:127:340:225:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:?:to take over the distressed project or not.
19:600:43106:22:18:114:540:203:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f5:A:–If the government provides a bailout, the healthy bank decides whether to use the
19:601:43188:18:17:127:316:185:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:?:cheaper funds to expand its project.9
19:602:43225:17:16:85:539:168:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:8We could additionally include distortionary e↵ects of transfers, as in Farhi and Tirole (2012). This is

19:605:43469:8:16:85:539:132:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:9Here the government is the leader in reacting when a bank is in distress. We also discuss later the results
19:606:43577:16:12:72:540:116:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:when the timing allows for healthy banks to takeover before governments decide bailouts, and still have the

20:613:44141:28:18:89:539:625:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The above timing of events applies to both the full information and the imperfect in-
20:614:44226:18:18:72:540:607:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:formation cases.  With full information, the government knows how many projects need

21:661:46733:38:18:72:540:473:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f5:B:Government PolicyThe government can modify the interest rate that banks face to

21:679:48303:12:12:71:539:165:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:strictly positive level of cash holdings of a bank. In a more general environment, a number of forces can break
21:680:48414:12:12:71:540:153:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the government’s indi↵erence between di↵erent ways of generating the same average interest rate towards

21:682:48624:12:12:71:539:129:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:distress, it would generate a strictly positive option value of waiting until the last possible moment before
21:683:48733:12:12:71:539:117:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:intervention. We do not explicitly incorporate these forces here, but we view our restriction on policies as
21:684:48841:12:0:71:218:105:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:motivated by such considerations.
22:685:48876:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank can take over the distressed project without the need of taxes. Denote the govern-

22:692:49417:18:18:72:346:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:function⇧(t, p),t2[1,2] which takes values in{0,1}.

22:704:50214:18:18:71:539:325:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:investment from taking over the distressed project, which is feasible using the proceeds from
22:705:50307:18:18:71:539:307:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:its successful project.  If a government bails out the first bank in distress, since bailouts

22:708:50570:18:18:71:545:254:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:1, this expansion is socially ine-cient because it generatesb⇢<1perunitofinvestment.
22:709:50654:18:18:72:540:236:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Hence, the cost of bailing out a bank when the shock is idiosyncratic is not only that the

22:711:50837:18:18:72:239:200:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:in socially ine-cient expansions.
22:712:50870:18:18:89:539:182:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:A:If the timing is expanded to allow for healthy banks to take over distressed projectsbefore
22:713:50961:18:18:72:539:164:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:governments decision about bailouts, then they would do so provided that⇢0+⇢1-1-b⇢-⇢0,
22:714:51047:18:18:72:540:146:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:i.e. when the gains from taking over privately are larger than the gains from expanding at a
22:715:51139:18:18:72:540:128:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:subsidized rate. In such case, government knows that a project showing distress is a sure sign
22:716:51233:18:18:72:540:110:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of an aggregate shock (since otherwise, the healthy bank would have taken over), and then
22:717:51322:18:0:72:539:92:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the full information analysis that we provide next applies. In contrast, if⇢0+⇢1-1<b⇢-⇢0,
23:718:51413:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:healthy banks would prefer to avoid taking over in order to push governments to believe they
23:719:51505:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:are facing an aggregate shock and then exploit the benefits from expanding at a subsidized
23:720:51595:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bailout rate. In this situation, governments would not be able to infer the health of the other
23:721:51690:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank when a projects shows distress, and then the imperfect information analysis that we

23:723:51799:18:18:89:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:This implies that our results are robust to such changes in the timing, provided that

27:886:61097:35:25:72:212:173:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f11:C:3.3.2  No Commitment
27:887:61117:25:18:72:540:148:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In this section we assume that the government is unable to commit to its policy announce-
27:888:61206:18:18:72:540:130:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ments. The banks internalize the government’s optimal ex-post actions in their optimization
27:889:61297:18:18:72:540:112:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:problem, e↵ectively making them first-movers and giving them the ability to choose the time
27:890:61388:18:0:72:297:94:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of the bailoutt⇤to maximize equation (10).
28:891:61432:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Definition 3 (Non-Commitment Equilibrium)A symmetric equilibrium without com-
28:892:61509:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:mitment is a cash choice of banksc⇤and a policy of the government⇧(t, p=1)such that
28:893:61592:18:18:72:539:671:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:given the banks’ choice of cash, the policy⇧(t, p=1)is the ex-post best response, and hence
28:894:61683:18:31:72:487:653:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:banks maximize (10) given the government’s reaction to both banks’ cash choices.
28:895:61763:31:18:89:539:622:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:As in the simple model, the government never intervenes in the case of an idiosyncratic
28:896:61850:18:18:72:539:604:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shock. This is becausey>x, and, in a symmetric equilibrium, takeover is feasible and so-
28:897:61938:18:18:72:540:586:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:cially preferable. In contrast, the government always intervenes when the shock is aggregate.
28:898:62031:18:18:72:540:568:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:This is becausex>0, and it is preferred to refinance the remainder of the project at a social
28:899:62124:18:18:72:171:550:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:cost than let it fail.
28:900:62146:18:18:89:539:532:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:How much do banks save att= 0 knowing this reaction of the government?  Under
28:901:62223:18:30:72:529:514:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Assumption 4, the unique non-commitment equilibrium is when all banks hold zero cash.
28:902:62308:30:18:72:539:484:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Proposition 3 (Optimal Policy without Commitment)Under Assumptions 2 and 4,
28:903:62383:18:18:72:540:466:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:the unique equilibrium without commitment is characterized by banks choosingc⇤=0, and
28:904:62468:18:31:71:423:448:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:the government immediately intervening when the shock is aggregate.
28:905:62535:31:18:89:539:417:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In what follows, we focus on the parameter space subset under which it is ex-ante optimal
28:906:62624:18:18:71:539:399:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:for governments to commit not bailing out banks in the aggregate state, but it is ex-post
28:907:62713:18:28:71:407:381:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:optimal for them to bail out banks in such a state, which implies:
28:908:62779:28:28:71:389:353:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:C:Assumption 5Ine-cient excessive leverage:1-⇢0⇢1<-<-⇤.
28:909:62832:28:18:89:539:325:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:This assumption, which combines Assumption 2 and Proposition 2, introduces into our
28:910:62915:18:18:71:539:307:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:model the tradeo↵we set out to study: the time-inconsistency of government policies. Ex-
28:911:63003:18:18:71:539:289:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ante the government would like to commit to no bailouts, but without commitment, there is
28:912:63092:18:18:71:540:271:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:excessive ine-cient leverage in the economy, with large projects but no liquidity to refinance
28:913:63186:18:17:71:539:253:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:in case both banks fail, with ine-cient bailouts on the equilibrium path. This assumption
28:914:63275:17:18:71:539:236:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:B:is more likely to hold whenP2is low,⇢1is low and⇡is relatively high with respect to⇢0.13
28:915:63363:18:16:81:539:218:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:13There are several ways this assumption may not hold. On the one hand, if-is either lower or higher
28:916:63463:16:15:72:540:202:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:than both cuto↵s-⇤and1-⇢0⇢1, then lack of commitment does not introduce any ine-ciency, rendering the
28:917:63564:15:12:71:540:187:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:problem irrelevant. On the other hand, if1-⇢0⇢1>->-⇤, it is ex-ante optimal for governments to commit
28:918:63665:12:11:71:539:175:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:to bailout banks when the shock is aggregate, but it is ex-post optimal not bailing out banks in such a state.
28:919:63775:11:12:71:540:164:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:In this last case there is ine-cient insu-cient liquidity and the strategic restraint mechanism we highlight
28:920:63883:12:0:71:374:152:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:in the next sections are not e↵ective to eliminate such an ine-ciency.
29:921:63955:0:30:72:445:707:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:4  Imperfect Information in the Full Model

31:989:68219:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:of financing the project until completion.  We will refer to equation (14) as thestrategic
31:990:68309:18:31:72:168:689:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f5:B:restraint condition.
31:991:68329:31:18:72:522:658:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f11:C:Proposition 4 (Equilibrium: No Commitment and Government Uncertainty)
31:992:68398:18:18:72:539:640:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:IfP02< ̄P2, there is a unique symmetric equilibrium wherec⇤=1-⇢0(i.e. ̄t(c⇤)=2),
31:993:68478:18:18:71:539:622:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:which coincides with the optimal solution under commitment. The equilibrium policy of the
31:994:68567:18:18:71:539:604:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f18:F:government is⇧(t, P02)=08tafter observing the first bank in distress, and⇧(t,1) = 18t
31:995:68652:18:31:72:290:586:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:after observing the second bank in distress.
31:996:68696:31:18:89:540:555:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:A:The statement of the proposition follows from applying thestrategic restraint condition
31:997:68783:18:18:72:539:537:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to all cases in which thedelayed bailout conditionholds. In all such cases, the value of being
31:998:68877:18:18:71:539:519:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the second bank in distress is discontinuously higher that the value of being the first bank
31:999:68969:18:17:71:539:501:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:in distress. Following a Bertrand-style undercutting argument, banks want to deviate from
31:1000:69058:17:18:71:544:484:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:asymmetricstrategyinordertoavoidbeingthefirst. At ̄t=2,thereisacornersolution
31:1001:69135:18:18:71:452:466:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and no more incentives to deviate, since banks can self-finance completely.
31:1002:69210:18:18:89:540:448:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The starkness of the above result relies on the discrete change in probabilities driven by
31:1003:69300:18:18:71:539:430:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:acontinuouschangeintheaction(cashc). This is certainly an extreme specification as
31:1004:69382:18:18:71:539:412:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:it requires that banks can perfectly control their time of distress by their cash choice. In
31:1005:69474:18:18:71:539:394:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the next subsection, we generalize our result to an environment with ex-post shocks to cash
31:1006:69565:18:18:71:539:376:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:holdings, such that small deviations in ex-ante cash choices do not guarantee a bank being
31:1007:69655:18:18:71:539:358:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:second in showing distress, only changing the relative position in a probabilistic way. We
31:1008:69745:18:18:71:539:340:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:derive an analogous result, showing that the Bertrand type competition still plays a role in
31:1009:69837:18:39:71:464:322:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bringing the equilibrium allocation closer to the optimum with commitment.

35:1212:76359:18:18:89:539:344:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Intuitively, from expression (18), the benefits from deviating and holding more cash than

35:1221:77093:45:30:72:263:156:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:5  Policy Implications
35:1222:77115:30:18:72:539:126:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:In the previous section, we showed thatgovernment uncertaintytogether withstrategic re-
35:1223:77202:18:0:71:539:108:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f5:B:strainthas the potential to implement e-cient commitment outcomes, even in the absence
36:1224:77290:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of commitment. Below, we study the impact of financial innovation, industry concentra-
36:1225:77376:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:tion, and asymmetric bank sizes on the potential of government uncertainty to induce more
36:1226:77465:18:39:72:323:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:e-cient outcomes in the absence of commitment.
36:1227:77511:39:26:72:253:632:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:C:5.1  Financial Innovation
36:1228:77536:26:18:72:540:606:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:This section analyzes how the information available to governments and the incentives of
36:1229:77624:18:18:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks change with the level of financial innovation in the economy that allows banks to
36:1230:77711:18:18:72:540:570:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:insure away part of their idiosyncratic risk. We allow banks to diversify their risk by holding
36:1231:77806:18:18:72:540:552:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:claims on other banks’ projects and selling a part of their own project. There are a number
36:1232:77897:18:17:72:540:534:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of financial arrangements that would achieve that goal. One is that banks sell a fraction of
36:1233:77989:17:18:72:540:517:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:claims on their project to a pool, and then hold the pool of the industry in proportions equal
36:1234:78083:18:18:72:547:499:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to their relative contributions by investing insecuritized assets.Moregenerallyonecould
36:1235:78170:18:18:71:540:481:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:consider many otherswaps and over-the-counter derivativesthat allow banks to cross-insure
36:1236:78259:18:18:72:539:463:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:each other’s cash flows, in order to get rid of some of the idiosyncratic risk of their project.
36:1237:78355:18:18:89:539:445:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We callsthe fraction of a project’s risk a bank can diversify away by using financial
36:1238:78440:18:18:72:544:427:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:instruments. We derive a cap ons,whichcanthenbemoregenerallythoughtofasacap
36:1239:78515:18:18:72:540:409:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:on the individual amount traded on financial instruments, that allow the government uncer-
36:1240:78605:18:18:72:540:391:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:tainty channel highlighted in this paper to keep operating to circumvent lack of commitment.
36:1241:78697:18:18:72:539:373:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:We use a securitization example to fix ideas, but the logic of this section can be applied more
36:1242:78792:18:18:72:432:355:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:broadly to any financial arrangement or innovation that diversify risk.
36:1243:78863:18:18:89:540:337:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Formally, the level of securitization is summarized by the fractionsof the project that a
36:1244:78952:18:18:71:539:319:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bank contributes to the pool and invests in the pool. For the case of two banks, for example,
36:1245:79045:18:18:71:543:301:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f5:B:s=1/2impliesthatthebankdiversifiesidiosyncraticriskscompletely,gettingtheaverage
36:1246:79125:18:18:71:539:283:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:return of the industry. Each bank is then responsible for financing the remaining fraction
36:1247:79215:18:17:71:194:265:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:1-sof its own project.
36:1248:79237:17:18:89:539:248:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:High level of securitization in the economy has the benefits of providing more diversifi-
36:1249:79326:18:18:71:539:230:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:cation to banks, which results in less need for accessing the market for additional funds. It
36:1250:79419:18:18:71:539:212:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:has, however, the cost of reducing the level of government uncertainty. In our setup, banks
36:1251:79510:18:18:71:539:194:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:are risk neutral and hence there are no benefits from diversification, but only costs in terms
36:1252:79604:18:18:71:386:176:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:B:of possibly inducing ine-cient, non-commitment, outcomes.16
36:1253:79663:18:18:89:540:158:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:First, we show that in our benchmark,anylevel of securitization completely removes
36:1254:79745:18:18:71:539:140:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:government uncertainty (Proposition 6). Then, we extend our benchmark setup to include
36:1255:79831:18:16:81:539:122:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:16Benefits of diversification are clearly important, but modeling them is outside the scope of this paper.
