39:1420:85797:39:25:72:231:225:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:C:5.2  Number of banks
39:1421:85817:25:18:72:540:200:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:In what follows we study the government incentives to bail out the first bank in distress
39:1422:85906:18:18:72:539:182:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:whenN>2. For any number of banks, not bailing out thefirstbank in distress is enough
39:1423:85990:18:18:72:540:164:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to trigger strategic restraints and obtain commitment-like outcomes. Below, we show that
39:1424:86078:18:18:72:540:146:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:having more banks in the economy reduces the incentives to bailout the first bank in distress
39:1425:86171:18:18:72:540:128:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:due to two forces. First, more banks increase the option value of waiting and learning about
39:1426:86263:18:18:72:540:110:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the true nature of the shock. Second, more banks may reduce the likelihood there is not a
39:1427:86352:18:0:72:537:92:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:healthy bank able to save the first bank in distress. We analyze these forces in turn below.
40:1428:86446:0:18:89:538:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f18:A:Denote byp(N,d)|sthe probability of havingdbanks in distress conditional on havingN
40:1429:86529:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:banks in total and observingsbank already showing distress. For example,p(2,2)|1⌘P02is
40:1430:86615:18:18:71:539:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the updated probability of an aggregate shock after observing one bank in distress from the
40:1431:86706:18:18:71:242:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:previous discussion whenN=2.
40:1432:86734:18:18:89:539:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We first consider a case in which the probability of an aggregate shock (allNbanks have
40:1433:86821:18:18:71:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:a liquidity shock) is independent ofN, and a counterfactual policy of bailing out for sure
40:1434:86911:18:18:71:539:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the second bank in distress. This case highlights an option value element in the incentives
40:1435:87002:18:31:71:277:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of the government to delay intervention.
40:1436:87042:31:18:71:539:550:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Lemma 3Letbx=0,p(N,N)|1=pfor allN. If the government bails out for sure the second
40:1437:87124:18:30:71:468:532:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:bank in distress, then the condition for delayed bailout isp<1-xyfor allN.
40:1438:87198:30:18:89:539:502:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:This Lemma is an important benchmark to understand the e↵ects ofNin the condition
40:1439:87279:18:18:71:539:484:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:for delay. Under the assumptions in the Lemma the number of banksNdoes not a↵ect the
40:1440:87363:18:18:71:539:466:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:conditions for delaying intervention on the first bank. This result, however depends on two
40:1441:87454:18:18:71:539:448:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:restrictions. First, the second bank in distress is bailed out. Second, the probability of an
40:1442:87547:18:18:71:359:430:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate shock is independent on the number of banks.
40:1443:87601:18:18:89:539:412:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In the next two lemmas we separately relax these two restrictions and isolate the two
40:1444:87686:18:18:71:539:394:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:forces for which more banks induce governments to delay intervention more likely.  The
40:1445:87772:18:18:71:544:376:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f16:B:first force is theoption value of waiting and seeing,whichworksthroughmakingthecuto↵
40:1446:87856:18:18:72:540:358:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of the delayed bailout condition increasing in the number of banks.  The second force is
40:1447:87944:18:18:72:546:340:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:more mechanical, alower likelihood of an aggregate shock,whichworksthroughmaking
40:1448:88024:18:18:72:540:322:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:governments more optimistic that there is at least some healthy bank able to take over the
40:1449:88114:18:31:72:325:304:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:first bank in distress when there are many banks.
40:1450:88163:31:18:72:540:273:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Lemma 4For allN, letbx=0,p(N,N)|1=p,p(N,N-1)|2,to=p0conditional on the first bank
40:1451:88244:18:17:72:540:255:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:being taken over (to) andp(N,N-1)|2,nto=1conditional on the first bank being not taken over
40:1452:88335:17:31:72:530:238:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:(nto). The delayed bailout condition of the first bank is more easily satisfied for largerN.
40:1453:88427:31:18:72:540:207:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Lemma 5Assumebx=0. Let1-↵be the probability of an aggregate shock, and if there is
40:1454:88509:18:18:71:540:189:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:no aggregate shock, let each bank have a liquidity shock with probability1--. Also, assume
40:1455:88599:18:18:71:539:171:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:F:governments always bailout second banks in distress. Then the probability to delay the bailout
40:1456:88693:18:31:71:339:153:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:of the first bank in distress weakly increases withN.
40:1457:88746:31:18:89:539:122:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The proofs of these three lemmas are in the Appendix. Their combination leads to the
40:1458:88830:18:0:71:179:104:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:following Proposition
41:1459:88853:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f11:143:g_d0_f17:F:Proposition 7The larger the number of banks in the economy, the more likely governments
41:1460:88940:18:31:71:346:689:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:delay interventions when banks start showing distress.
41:1461:88994:31:18:89:540:658:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:In words, a larger number of banks introduce two forces that delay government interven-
41:1462:89081:18:18:71:539:640:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:tion and lead to strategic restraints. Lemma 3 shows a benchmark, under which the number
41:1463:89169:18:18:71:540:622:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:of banks does not a↵ect the probability of an aggregate shock and does not a↵ect the option
41:1464:89260:18:18:72:539:604:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:value of delaying, since we impose bailouts of a second bank shows distress. In this case, the
41:1465:89354:18:18:72:486:586:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:government’s incentives to delay bailouts is independent of the number of banks.
41:1466:89434:18:18:89:539:568:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Lemma 4 relaxes the assumption that governments have to intervene if a second bank is
41:1467:89519:18:17:72:540:550:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:in distress. This introduces the option value of not bailing out the first bank and having the
41:1468:89613:17:18:72:540:533:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:chance to make the optimal decision of not bailing out if other banks show distress. This
41:1469:89702:18:18:72:540:515:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Lemma shows that more banks makes more valuable the option value of learning and making
41:1470:89789:18:18:72:196:497:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:better decisions ex-post.
41:1471:89814:18:18:89:539:479:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Lemma 5 relaxes the assumption that the probability of an aggregate shock is independent
41:1472:89902:18:18:72:539:461:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ofN. E↵ectively, it is less likely that no bank is healthy when there are many banks, and
41:1473:89991:18:18:72:540:443:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:then less likely that the first bank in distress is not taken over and fails in case of not being
41:1474:90088:18:18:72:226:425:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bailed out by the government.
41:1475:90117:18:18:89:539:407:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:These last two forces complement each other. When there are many banks in the industry
41:1476:90203:18:18:72:540:389:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and a bank shows distress, it is less likely it fails if not bailed out and it is more valuable for
41:1477:90302:18:39:72:221:371:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:governments to wait and see.
41:1478:90330:39:25:72:276:332:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:C:5.3  Asymmetric Bank Sizes

41:1480:90448:18:18:72:545:289:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:bailouts.  Our goal is to analyze the impact oftoo big to fail banks,thisisbankswhose

42:1547:92626:18:18:72:540:285:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to a new and unique negative externality of ‘too big to fail’ banks for households, who may
42:1548:92717:18:45:72:512:267:143:g_d0_f5:64:g_d0_f12:B:not only need to bailout large banks but also excessive risk exposure of small banks.18
42:1549:92804:45:30:72:201:222:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:6  Conclusions
42:1550:92818:30:18:72:540:192:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:At the onset of financial crises, banks usually tend to show distress sequentially.  Then,
42:1551:92908:18:18:72:540:174:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:initially, when deciding whether to intervene or not, governments are uncertain about the
42:1552:92997:18:17:72:540:156:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:nature of the problem at hand. We show that suchgovernment uncertaintyleads governments
42:1553:93084:17:18:72:540:139:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:to delay bailouts in order to learn further about the nature of the underlying situation
42:1554:93172:18:16:81:540:121:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:18Since the payo↵function for Bank 2 is discontinuous atc2= 0, its supremum is not attainable. Still, if
42:1555:93276:16:12:71:539:105:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:cash is discretely undivisible, then the cash holding of Bank 2 is given by one unit of cash, regardless of how
42:1556:93387:12:0:71:217:93:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:small the unit of measurement is.
43:1557:93422:0:18:72:540:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:from market outcomes. Crucially, such delays introduce incentives for banks to compete,
43:1558:93509:18:18:72:540:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:in Bertrand-style fashion, for their relative performance, giving rise to endogenousstrategic
43:1559:93602:18:18:72:431:671:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f5:B:restraintof their levels of risk taking and exposure to liquidity shocks.
43:1560:93675:18:18:89:539:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:We show that these novel forces have dramatic e↵ects on the equilibrium outcomes in
43:1561:93758:18:18:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the economy. In seminal models of banking and liquidity choices, Holmstr ̈om and Tirole
43:1562:93845:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:(1998) and Farhi and Tirole (2012) show that no commitment can lead to endogenous crises
43:1563:93933:18:18:72:539:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:and ine-cient bailouts. Modellinggovernment uncertaintyradically changes these results,
43:1564:94020:18:18:72:540:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:moving the economy from ine-ciently high levels of leverage to e-cient levels, even in the
43:1565:94110:18:18:72:196:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:absence of commitment.
43:1566:94132:18:18:89:540:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Based on these insights we provide a novel discussion of how financial innovations, bank-
43:1567:94221:18:18:72:540:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ing concentration and asymmetric bank sizes can induce endogenous systemic events. In our
43:1568:94310:18:18:72:540:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:case this works through the e↵ects of these aspects of the banking industry on the inference
43:1569:94402:18:17:72:441:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:problem of the government and the ensuing strategic behavior of banks.
43:1570:94472:17:18:89:540:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:The literature has identified the time-inconsistency of governments’ policies as an impor-
43:1571:94562:18:18:72:540:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:tant justification for macro-prudential regulation and direct overseeing of banks’ activities.
43:1572:94656:18:18:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:However, historically regulators have been incapable to design macro-prudential regulation
43:1573:94746:18:18:72:540:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:that prevents crises without choking o↵growth. Our work suggests that it may be optimal
43:1574:94833:18:18:72:540:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:for governments to design political structures that delay bailouts decisions, or regulatory
43:1575:94924:18:18:72:540:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:standards that maintain an optimal level of uncertainty, imposing lower burdens on pre-
43:1576:95011:18:18:72:540:366:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:ventive regulation and giving more room to facilitate optimal self-regulation. Contrary to
43:1577:95101:18:18:72:540:348:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the common view that information and speed of action are desirable characteristics of pol-
43:1578:95191:18:18:72:540:330:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:icymakers, it may be the case that banks’ perception about policymakers reacting fast to
43:1579:95279:18:18:72:540:312:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:systemic events give them incentives to coordinate on those, endogenously generating crises.
43:1580:95371:18:18:89:539:294:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Our framework can be extended in several directions to address other interesting questions
43:1581:95461:18:18:72:540:276:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:regarding bank bailouts, information frictions and time consistency. One natural extension of
43:1582:95554:18:18:72:539:258:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f17:B:our analysis is to include the possibility of contagion, where a failure of one bank maytrigger
43:1583:95649:18:18:72:540:240:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the need for refinancing of other banks. Our benchmark model can be easily extended to
43:1584:95735:18:17:72:540:222:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:include an exogenous probability of contagion, interpreted as an increase in the probability of
43:1585:95830:17:18:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:an aggregate shock, conditional on one project failing. This possibility lowers the probability
43:1586:95925:18:18:72:540:187:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:that there will be enough liquidity in the system if the first bank in distress is allowed to
43:1587:96018:18:18:72:540:169:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:fail, which reduces the incentives of the government to delay bailouts, making commitment
43:1588:96107:18:18:72:540:151:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:outcomes harder to obtain.19This is naturally a very crude way of thinking about contagion.
43:1589:96198:18:15:81:539:133:49:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:19Formally, we can modify the benchmark model’s stochastic structure by introducing a probability-that
43:1590:96300:15:12:72:540:118:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the situation is contagious. This can be modeled as an increase in the probability of an aggregate shock from
43:1591:96409:12:12:72:540:106:99:g_d0_f23:99:g_d0_f8:F:P2toP2+-, conditional on one project failing. If the contagion shock is independent of the other refinancing
43:1592:96517:12:0:72:539:94:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:shocks, then the delayed bailout condition becomesbP02=P2+-P1+P2+->P02, meaning that the delayed bailout
44:1593:96623:0:18:72:533:707:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:Modeling its micro-foundations may be important in evaluating the welfare costs of delay.
44:1594:96712:18:18:89:539:689:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Another avenue to explore is the solvency versus liquidity nature of banks’ distress.
44:1595:96797:18:18:72:540:671:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:This particular uncertainty always haunt governments when there are bank runs, since their
44:1596:96887:18:18:72:540:653:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:optimal response depends on the nature of the distress. In case of insolvency, the bank should
44:1597:96981:18:18:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:be wound down; in case of illiquidity, its assets should be replenished. Our model in this
44:1598:97071:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:paper is not equipped to address this issue. By assumption, the project size deterministically
44:1599:97165:18:18:72:540:599:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:determines the speed of cash outflows of the project, and every time the project needs
44:1600:97251:18:18:72:540:581:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:refinancing, it is still a positive net present value investment. Hence, all shocks are liquidity
44:1601:97348:18:18:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:shocks.  In ongoing work, we explore an alternative environment in which the inference
44:1602:97434:18:18:72:540:545:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:problem of the government is about finding out whether the underlying problem of the bank
44:1603:97523:18:18:72:515:527:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:is insolvency or illiquidity, and then deciding whether to save the project at all or not.
44:1604:97613:18:18:89:539:509:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:A:Finally, in this paper we focus solely on risk-free loans, where banks cannot default on
44:1605:97701:18:17:72:540:491:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:their debt.  Hence, all bailouts in the model are bailouts of equity holders and not debt
44:1606:97790:17:18:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:holders. In an extension that allows for default, interest rates would include a premium for
44:1607:97882:18:18:72:540:456:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the expected probability of default, which clearly depends on whether a bailout to lenders is
44:1608:97975:18:18:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:expected in case of default. If banks and lenders expect bailouts in case of a systemic event,
44:1609:98069:18:18:72:539:420:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:the premium is low and there is e↵ectively a subsidy to risk taking, possibly inducing exces-
44:1610:98162:18:18:72:540:402:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:sive leverage and endogenous crises. This extension needs further analysis, but it clarifies
44:1611:98254:18:45:72:530:384:143:g_d0_f5:143:g_d0_f5:B:that restricting the model to bailing out only equity holders is not critical for our results.
44:1612:98348:45:30:72:163:339:296:g_d0_f11:296:g_d0_f11:C:References
